Direct old-ABI CFF helpers with descriptor `(JIIIII[J)J` were also unique: TEST `170/170`, evaluator `122/122`, and obfusjack `275/275`. Full family rows were SnakeGame `__neko_cff$ 59/59`, `__neko_cff_xmat$ 7/7`, `__neko_cff_xmat_init$ 3/3`, `__neko_cff_tmat_init$ 10/10`; TEST `170/170`, `34/34`, `8/8`, `42/42`; evaluator `122/122`, `29/29`, `6/6`, `49/49`; obfusjack `275/275`, `18/18`, `7/7`, `34/34`. Therefore current CFF helper reduction cannot be achieved by exact body sharing; it requires a new architecture-level materialization/dispatch compression route.

- [ ] Subtask 7DL: Post-7DH/7DK objective-gap audit before the next architecture route.
  - Scope: map the current freshly generated full-JVM helper topology back to the active objective after exact string and CFF body sharing have both been exhausted. This audit must not change production source behavior. It must identify the largest remaining helper families and distinguish runtime helper surfaces from `<clinit>` materialization/init surfaces.
  - Required evidence: 7DH reduced no-internal string concat helpers and 7DJ proved no exact `__neko_strcat$` duplicate bodies remain. 7DF reduced direct CFF wrapper helpers and 7DK proved the current CFF helper families have no exact duplicate bodies. The next production change must therefore be an architecture-level materialization/dispatch compression route rather than another cache-key or exact-body sharing attempt.
  - Validation command/runtime target: inspect current `build/test-jvm-full-obf-perf/*-full-jvm-obf.jar.map`, helper stats, and latest perf/marker outputs only. Do not run the full test suite.
  - Completion criteria: record which remaining helper family or materialization path is the next justified target, and explicitly block routes already disproven by 7DJ/7DK unless new evidence appears.
  - Completion evidence: current helper-family exact-sharing routes are exhausted by 7DJ/7DK, and the largest remaining source-visible materialization surface is `<clinit>` CFF material init, not string concat or indy singleton helpers. Current `__neko_cff_xmat_init$` stats are SnakeGame `3 / 31135` bytes, TEST `8 / 115823`, evaluator `6 / 65380`, and obfusjack `7 / 113229`; current `__neko_cff_tmat_init$` stats are SnakeGame `10 / 64812`, TEST `42 / 226702`, evaluator `49 / 381746`, and obfusjack `34 / 263147`. By contrast current obfusjack `__neko_strcat$` is only `31 / 2290` bytes and 7DJ proved it has no duplicate bodies. The next justified target is therefore generic CFF material init compression: reduce repeated literal `int` push/store bytecode in cinit material registration while keeping encrypted object-array material, live runtime flowkey decoding, no static decrypt of application data, and no fallback path.

- [x] Subtask 7DM: Pack CFF material init int stores through a shared cinit-only pair store helper.
  - Scope: compress CFF token/transition material init helpers by replacing pairs of literal `int` material stores with one packed `long` constant plus a shared generated cinit-only helper that writes the two int words into the existing class-owned material `int[]`. This targets only `<clinit>` material registration size. It must not change transition/token material row semantics, runtime material decode, live flowkey/method-key dependency, CFF block construction, helper callsite descriptors, string helpers, indy helpers, or runtime fallback behavior.
  - Required evidence: 7DL identifies `__neko_cff_xmat_init$` and `__neko_cff_tmat_init$` as the largest remaining helper/materialization bytecode surfaces. Each row is currently emitted as many repeated `ALOAD material; push index; push int value; IASTORE` sequences. Packing two opaque encrypted/mask material words into one long constant reduces repeated literal store bytecode while still registering the same material into the existing object-array backing arrays before runtime.
  - Validation command/runtime target: refresh `neko-transforms` with manual `javac`, run the manual targeted JUnit Launcher classes `JvmStringObfuscationIntegrationTest`, `JvmInvokeDynamicObfuscationIntegrationTest`, `ControlFlowFlatteningAlgebraicAuditTest`, `CffStrongEntrySeedRegressionTest`, and `JvmFullObfuscationPerfTest`, then inspect forbidden markers, missing-flowkey `keyed=0`, helper API, output size, material init helper stats, and TEST/obfusjack timing. Do not run the full test suite.
  - Completion criteria: accept only if targeted validation passes, no `MethodTooLarge` or forbidden marker appears, missing-flowkey rows remain `keyed=0`, material init helper size or output size improves, runtime flowkey-dependent decode remains unchanged, and no plaintext/static decrypt/fallback path is introduced.
  - Completion evidence: rejected and reverted. The attempted implementation installed a generated shared `__neko_cff_imat$` cinit-only helper with descriptor `([IIJ)V` and changed token/transition material init emission to packed-pair stores. Manual `neko-transforms` compilation passed, but the targeted JVM obfuscation JUnit run failed in `JvmFullObfuscationPerfTest` while writing the fresh obfusjack artifact: `org.objectweb.asm.MethodTooLargeException: Method too large: a/a.main ([Ljava/lang/String;)V`, with diagnostics reporting `65880 bytes estimated  main([Ljava/lang/String;)V` and `54668 bytes estimated  <clinit>()V`. The route violates 7DM completion criteria (`MethodTooLarge` must reject) and is not retained. Runtime flowkey-dependent decode was not changed in the reverted source, and no static decrypt/fallback path is accepted from this attempt.
  - Post-revert evidence: after reverting the source change, manual `neko-transforms` compilation passed and a single targeted `JvmFullObfuscationPerfTest` rerun passed with `testsStarted=1 testsSucceeded=1`. The refreshed obfusjack artifact has `Control-flow generated helpers missing flow keys: candidates=63 keyed=0`, generated helper API `methods=390 fields=18`, and forbidden marker scan clean. Current obfusjack material init helper stats remain `__neko_cff_tmat_init$ total=34 sizeSum=263150` and `__neko_cff_xmat_init$ total=7 sizeSum=113185`, so the rejected pair-store helper left no accepted production route.

- [x] Subtask 7DN: Audit string/indy helper registration surfaces for static-key-shaped duplication.
  - Scope: inspect the current string and invokedynamic JVM transform helper registration paths that still emit multiple same-structure helpers differentiated by static key material. The audit must distinguish helpers whose bytecode is already exact-body unique from helpers whose only meaningful differences are embedded key constants, descriptors, or per-site registration constants. This is an evidence step only unless the audit identifies one generic architecture-level route.
  - Required evidence: 7DJ proved current no-internal `__neko_strcat$` helpers have no exact duplicate bodies, and 7DK proved current CFF helper exact-body sharing is exhausted. The user objective still explicitly calls out indy/string decrypt helper registrations and requires moving static helper/key material toward dynamic dispatch and cinit object-array material without static decrypt. Any accepted next route must preserve live flowkey/method-key dependency, avoid self-canceling key logic, keep strings/indy protected by existing obfuscation surfaces, and introduce no fallback/original-call path.
  - Completion evidence: current refreshed obfusjack artifact has `__neko_indy` helper total `20`, size sum `2244` bytes, and exact-body census `total=20 uniqueBodies=20 duplicateGroups=0 duplicateMethods=0`. The only repeated-looking indy surface is the per-class bootstrap trampoline, each about `13` bytes, which loads that class's existing CFF object-array carrier and calls the shared package helper; the real shared indy core/resolve/flow/guard helpers already live in one owner. Current obfusjack `__neko_str` helper total is `32`, size sum `10326` bytes, with exact-body census `total=32 uniqueBodies=32 duplicateGroups=0 duplicateMethods=0`; current `__neko_strcat$` remains `31/31` unique. The largest string helper is the shared decode helper with descriptor `([Ljava/lang/Object;IJI)Ljava/lang/String;`, already taking the object-array carrier directly. Therefore current string/indy exact helper consolidation is not a justified implementation target: there is no proven generic duplicate helper body or static-key-only helper family to merge without adding a new lookup/adapter path. The remaining objective-relevant size surface remains CFF material registration/init, not string/indy helper registration.

- [x] Subtask 7DO: Audit packed CFF material representation instead of pair-store helper emission.
  - Scope: evaluate whether CFF token/transition material can be represented as packed `long[]` rows inside the existing class-owned object-array material carrier, with runtime material word reads unpacking high/low int words under the existing live flowkey-dependent decode path. This is different from rejected 7DM: it must not add cinit pair-store invocations or per-row helper calls, and it must target the material representation itself.
  - Required evidence: 7DM proved helper-call based pair-store compression increases method size enough to trigger `MethodTooLarge` on fresh obfusjack. Current material init stats still show `__neko_cff_tmat_init$ total=34 sizeSum=263150` and `__neko_cff_xmat_init$ total=7 sizeSum=113185`, with `avgLongPush=0.0` and thousands of repeated int pushes/stores. A viable next route must reduce repeated cinit material stores without reducing CFF block coverage, without moving decode to static plaintext, and without changing dynamic flowkey/method-key dependence.
  - Validation command/runtime target: source inspection first, then if implemented compile `neko-transforms` manually and run only JVM obfuscation targeted tests including `JvmFullObfuscationPerfTest`. Inspect forbidden markers, missing-flowkey `keyed=0`, generated helper API, output size, material init stats, and TEST/obfusjack timing. Do not run the full test suite.
  - Completion criteria: either record a concrete generic implementation path for packed material representation, or reject it with exact source/runtime evidence. Any accepted implementation must keep token/transition material encrypted/opaque in the object-array carrier, keep runtime decode driven by live flowkey/method-key state, avoid self-canceling key logic, avoid static decrypt, and introduce no fallback/original-bytecode path.
  - Implementation state: source inspection identified a generic path that preserves external helper ABI: allocate token/transition material as packed `long[]` rows in the existing object-array carrier, emit cinit material stores as packed high/low int words, keep row starts aligned with one padding word for odd row widths, and update only the internal material word-load emitters to unpack high/low words at runtime. This changes material representation, not CFF block construction, direct helper descriptors, or flowkey/method-key transfer.
  - Runtime narrowing: the first implementation packed both token and transition material. It passed targeted JVM tests and reduced output/material-init size, but runtime evidence showed unacceptable hot-path regression in obfusjack (`Seq: 440 ms`, `VThreads: 727 ms`) because transition material is decoded on CFF transition paths. The retained implementation is narrowed to token material only; transition material stays `int[]` to preserve hot transition performance while still reducing cinit token material size.
  - Completion evidence: accepted token-only packed material implementation. Manual `neko-transforms` compilation passed. Targeted JVM obfuscation tests only passed with `testsFound=7 testsStarted=7 testsSucceeded=7 testsFailed=0` for `JvmStringObfuscationIntegrationTest`, `JvmInvokeDynamicObfuscationIntegrationTest`, `ControlFlowFlatteningAlgebraicAuditTest`, `CffStrongEntrySeedRegressionTest`, and `JvmFullObfuscationPerfTest`. Forbidden marker scan is clean. Refreshed obfusjack hardening remains `Control-flow generated helpers missing flow keys: candidates=63 keyed=0` and generated helper API remains `methods=390 fields=18`. Output size improved versus post-revert baseline: TEST `775309 -> 720861`, obfusjack `747687 -> 685680`, SnakeGame `230930 -> 214426`, evaluator `1044179 -> 960793`. Current material init stats show token init reduction while transition init remains on the original int hot path: obfusjack `__neko_cff_tmat_init$ total=34 sizeSum=142236` versus post-revert `263150`, and `__neko_cff_xmat_init$ total=7 sizeSum=113222` versus post-revert `113185`. Runtime hot-path regression from full packing is removed: obfusjack full-obf timing is `Platform threads: 43 ms`, `Virtual threads: 47 ms`, `Seq: 254 ms`, `Parallel: 7 ms`, `VThreads: 9 ms`, comparable to or better than post-revert `47/47/257/8/11`; TEST Calc is `171ms` versus post-revert `173ms`. The retained change does not add fallback, static decrypt, original-bytecode fallback, or descriptor changes; token material remains opaque in the existing object-array carrier and is decoded through the existing live guard/path/block flowkey-dependent token helper.

Inspect forbidden markers, missing-flowkey `keyed=0`, helper API, direct helper count, output size, `MethodTooLarge`, and TEST/obfusjack timings. Do not run the full test suite.
  - Completion criteria: either record a concrete generic implementation path for direct-helper material-table conversion, or reject it with exact evidence. Any accepted path must not introduce static decrypt, static key recomputation, self-canceling key logic, fallback/original-bytecode path, Java helper layer, descriptor downgrade, CFF coverage reduction, or hot-path performance regression.
  - Completion evidence: audited and not implemented in this subtask. Source inspection shows the current `__neko_cff$` family is generated by `TransitionOutliner.createIslandDispatchHelper`, not by the dead transition wrapper branch. The dead wrapper branch is `createHelper`, but `emitCall` currently sets `materialTransition = true` and routes outlined transitions through `registerTransitionMaterialRow` plus the class `__neko_cff_xmat$` material helper. The live `__neko_cff$` helpers are island-dispatch helpers: each helper builds per-island token dispatch cases, fake labels, result tokens, bounce tokens, poison logic, and calls `finishOutlinedDispatchReturn` to write live transition output before returning the live method key. Current artifact evidence confirms they are not duplicate static-key helper bodies: obfusjack `__neko_cff$ total=275 uniqueBodies=275 duplicateGroups=0 duplicateMethods=0`, with `sizeSum=122035`, `max=930`. Therefore 7DU does not accept a direct implementation: converting this family requires a new table-driven island-dispatch architecture that materializes per-island cases/result tokens/fake bounce metadata into the object-array material path and proves the shared dispatcher preserves live key flow and CFF dispatch semantics. This is a separate high-risk architecture task, not an exact sharing/chunking fix. Blocked shortcut routes: deleting `createHelper` does not affect generated artifacts; further init chunk coarsening is blocked by 7DS/7DT method-size evidence; merging `__neko_cff$` helpers by exact body is blocked by unique-body evidence; inlining helpers would reduce helper count by moving code back into protected methods and would not satisfy the size/JIT objective without new proof.

- [x] Subtask 7DV: Design table-driven CFF island dispatch materialization before implementation.
  - Scope: produce an implementation design for replacing live `__neko_cff$` island-dispatch helper proliferation with a material-backed shared island dispatcher, if and only if the design can preserve full-strength CFF semantics and live key flow. This is a design/evidence subtask; do not edit production source until the design records exact material rows, call ABI, runtime validation target, and proof obligations.
  - Required evidence: 7DU identifies the real `__neko_cff$` source as `createIslandDispatchHelper`, including dispatch cases, fake cases, result tokens, bounce tokens, poison path, and transition output writes. A correct design must cover each of those without static decrypt, static key recomputation, descriptor-only recomputation, self-canceling key logic, fallback, reduced block granularity, or changed CFF coverage.
  - Validation command/runtime target: source inspection and artifact stats first. If a design is later implemented, validation must include manual `neko-transforms` compilation, the targeted JVM obfuscation tests, forbidden marker scan, hardening `keyed=0`, helper API/direct helper count, output size, method-size diagnostics, and TEST/obfusjack timings. Do not run the full test suite.
  - Completion criteria: either record a concrete low-risk implementation plan with exact data layout and runtime proof path, or reject table-driven island dispatch for the current task with exact evidence.
  - Completion evidence: rejected for immediate implementation. A fully shared material-backed island dispatcher would need to externalize each island's case tokens, fake-case descriptors, bounce token, result tokens, dense/sparse router mode, poison behavior, and transition output writes into object-array material. That preserves data availability, but it changes the runtime dispatch mechanism: current `createIslandDispatchHelper` emits per-island bytecode switches through `emitTokenDispatch`, whereas a shared helper would need either a material-table linear/binary search or a new indirect dispatch structure. This would move a hot CFF dispatch path from JVM `lookupswitch/tableswitch` bytecode into runtime table probing and risks the same kind of performance regression already observed for full transition material packing. A shared helper descriptor would also need an additional island/material row id or equivalent encoded input, which is a generated-internal ABI change requiring new hardening metadata and validation. Because current `__neko_cff$` helpers are small (`obfusjack max=930`) and exact-body unique (`275/275`), this route is not a low-risk implementation without a separate prototype and proof. It is therefore blocked for this task by hot-path performance risk and incomplete proof, not by missing source access.

- [x] Subtask 7DW: Audit trivial CFF island-dispatch helper bypass as a bounded helper-count route.
  - Scope: determine whether a subset of `__neko_cff$` island-dispatch helpers can be avoided for trivial islands without converting all dispatch to a table-driven shared helper. Candidate cases are islands whose generated helper would contain no fake cases and one real block, where the caller could directly write the same transition output and route result without a helper call. This audit must not change CFF block construction, block granularity, dynamic key flow, or transition semantics.
  - Required evidence: 7DV blocks full table-driven shared dispatch as too risky. The remaining possible low-risk route is a narrow bypass for trivial helpers, but only if source inspection proves the helper's behavior is exactly equivalent to caller-side `finishOutlinedDispatchReturn` plus existing result router, and artifact/source evidence proves the caller method has enough method-size headroom.
  - Validation command/runtime target: source inspection first. If implemented, manually compile `neko-transforms`, run only targeted JVM obfuscation tests, inspect forbidden markers, missing-flowkey `keyed=0`, helper API/direct helper count, output size, `MethodTooLarge`, and TEST/obfusjack timings. Do not run the full test suite.
  - Completion criteria: either implement a strictly bounded bypass with proof and validation, or reject it with exact evidence. It must not introduce fallback, static key material exposure, descriptor downgrades, self-canceling key logic, CFF coverage reduction, or method-size regression.
  - Completion evidence: rejected for immediate implementation. The candidate bypass is not equivalent to removing a call: caller-side island labels currently invoke a generated island helper, store the returned live method key, then reload guard/path/block/pc/domain from the shared `outLocal` transition array. The helper itself performs token dispatch, real/fake case handling, poison handling, and `finishOutlinedDispatchReturn`, which writes the same `outLocal` state expected by the caller's uniform continuation. Inlining even "trivial" helpers would move dispatch switch/fake/poison/result-write bytecode back into the protected caller method, increasing the exact method-size pressure that outliners are intended to avoid. Artifact inspection of current obfusjack shows the caller contains many `invokestatic ... (JIIIII[J)J` CFF dispatch calls, while current `__neko_cff$` helpers are individually small (`min=240`, `p50=436`, `max=930`) but numerous. No exact source/artifact evidence proves sufficient caller method-size headroom for safe inlining, and previous runs have already hit `MethodTooLarge` on related CFF-size changes. Therefore this route is blocked without a dedicated method-size estimator/prototype. It is not implemented.

- [x] Subtask 7DX: Define the remaining required architecture prototype for CFF island-dispatch reduction.
  - Scope: summarize the remaining work required to reduce the live `__neko_cff$` island-dispatch helper surface after all low-risk chunking, exact-sharing, string/indy, and trivial-bypass routes have been exhausted.
  - Required evidence: use 7DT, 7DU, and 7DW evidence to define the next prototype's prerequisites and validation gates.
  - Validation command/runtime target: planning only. No source edit or tests.
  - Completion criteria: record the prototype boundary clearly enough that implementation does not proceed without a method-size estimator, runtime dispatch proof, and targeted validation plan.
  - Completion evidence: the remaining objective work is now bounded to a separate CFF island-dispatch architecture prototype. Prerequisites before implementation: (1) add or reuse a bytecode method-size estimator for protected caller methods and generated island helpers, because helper bypass/inlining can reintroduce `MethodTooLarge`; (2) define a material layout for island dispatch metadata that covers dispatch tokens, fake cases, bounce tokens, result tokens, dense/sparse route mode, poison behavior, and transition output writes; (3) define a shared dispatcher ABI that preserves live method-key local publication for hardening and does not downgrade generated internal descriptors into static-key recomputation; (4) prove the runtime dispatcher remains driven by live guard/path/block/pc/method-key state and does not use self-canceling/static key material; (5) benchmark the hot CFF dispatch path before accepting, because full transition material packing already proved that size reductions can regress obfusjack runtime. Current blocked shortcut routes are explicitly closed: string/indy exact helper sharing has no duplicate bodies; token/transition init chunking is at method-size boundary; `__neko_cff$` exact sharing has no duplicate bodies; dead transition wrapper cleanup would not change artifacts; trivial helper bypass lacks caller method-size proof. Therefore no further production source change is justified under the current evidence chain without first building this prototype and validation scaffold.

- [x] Subtask 7DY: Method-size estimator prerequisite audit for CFF island-dispatch prototype.
  - Scope: determine whether the next architecture prototype needs a new production method-size estimator or can reuse existing artifact-level tooling, and identify the exact estimator gap before any island-dispatch implementation.
  - Required evidence: 7DW blocks helper bypass because caller method-size headroom is not proven, and prior runs have produced `MethodTooLarge` when a CFF/material route increased method size. A valid prerequisite must distinguish current artifact-size measurement from pre-implementation caller growth prediction.
  - Validation command/runtime target: planning/audit only. No production source edit and no full test suite.
  - Completion criteria: record whether an estimator exists, what it covers, what it does not cover, and what a future prototype must add before changing CFF island dispatch.
  - Completion evidence: accepted as audit-only. Existing `HelperMethodStats` already reuses ASM code-size evaluation for generated artifacts and has repeatedly provided concrete method-size evidence (`__neko_cff_tmat_init$`, `__neko_cff_xmat_init$`, `__neko_cff$`, string, indy). Adding a conservative production guard now is not justified: it could hard-reject jars that the JVM would still accept, and it would not reduce helper registration. The uncovered prerequisite is pre-change caller growth estimation: before any `__neko_cff$` bypass or table-driven prototype, the transform needs a dry-run estimator for the protected caller method after hypothetical inline/bypass code insertion, plus generated helper size estimates, so the prototype can prove it will not reintroduce `MethodTooLarge`. Therefore no production source edit is made in 7DY; the future prototype must first add or script a dry-run estimator that models caller growth and validates against `HelperMethodStats` on fresh artifacts.

- [x] Subtask 7DZ: Prototype trivial-island census without production changes.
  - Scope: count how many `__neko_cff$` island-dispatch helpers might be trivial enough for a future bypass, without editing production code. This should determine whether a bypass prototype is worth building.
  - Required evidence: 7DW rejected immediate bypass because no caller-size proof exists. Before building a dry-run estimator, determine whether there is enough potential payoff by measuring the current helper-size distribution and identifying low-size helper buckets as candidate trivial islands.
  - Validation command/runtime target: artifact inspection only using current full-JVM jars/maps and helper stats. Do not run the full test suite.
  - Completion criteria: record candidate payoff. If the candidate surface is small, reject bypass-prototype priority; if large, define the estimator/prototype as the next implementation task.
  - Completion evidence: accepted as artifact-only audit and rejected as an implementation trigger. Current obfusjack `__neko_cff$` helper stats show a large remaining surface (`total=275`, `sizeSum=122035`, `min=240`, `p50=436`, `p90=614`, `max=930`), and exact-body census remains `total=275 uniqueBodies=275 duplicateGroups=0 duplicateMethods=0`. This proves helper-count payoff exists in aggregate, but the artifact-only size buckets do not prove trivial-island semantics. A small helper can still contain token dispatch, fake/poison paths, result-token writes, and the required `outLocal` transition-output protocol; the jar/map names and bytecode size alone do not encode `fakeCount`, island real-block count, dense/sparse routing mode, or caller method-size headroom. Therefore no production bypass is justified from 7DZ evidence. The next valid route is a source-level dry-run estimator/prototype that tags island metadata before generation, estimates protected caller growth, preserves live `flowkey`/method-key dependence through the existing `outLocal` protocol, and rejects any static decrypt, static key recomputation, self-canceling key logic, fallback, CFF coverage reduction, or `MethodTooLarge` regression.

- [x] Subtask 7EA: Implement source-level CFF island dry-run estimator without changing generated semantics.

This subtask must not remove helpers, inline island dispatch, alter CFF block construction, alter token/fake/poison/result routing, change generated descriptors, weaken hidden-key ABI, introduce static decrypt/static keys, or replace live `flowkey`/method-key propagation.

  - Validation command/runtime target: manually compile only the affected transform classes first. Any later implementation still requires a separate subtask and must preserve strong live `flowkey` dependence with no static decrypt or fallback.
  - Completion evidence: accepted. Added a source-level CFF island dry-run estimator that records per-method and aggregate island-helper counts in `PipelineContext` under `controlFlowFlattening.islandDryRunStats`, and emits diagnostic counts from the CFF pass. The estimator is attached after the existing island helper and callsite are generated, so the generated semantics remain unchanged: helpers are still emitted by `createIslandDispatchHelper`, helper flowkey locals are still published, caller bytecode still invokes the helper, stores the returned live method key, reloads `outLocal`, and routes through the existing result router. The estimator records real-block count, fake-case count, dense/sparse router mode, result token count, dispatch case count, helper instruction count, callsite instruction count, and minimum caller-growth estimate. It does not emit or persist key material, seed material, material-table contents, plaintext metadata, static decrypt state, fallback state, or helper-layer rescue data. Manual `neko-transforms` compilation passed. Targeted JVM-obfuscation validation only passed through Gradle for `JvmStringObfuscationIntegrationTest`, `JvmInvokeDynamicObfuscationIntegrationTest`, `ControlFlowFlatteningAlgebraicAuditTest`, `CffStrongEntrySeedRegressionTest`, and `JvmFullObfuscationPerfTest`; no full test suite was run. The first sandboxed Gradle attempts failed before test execution because Gradle could not open a local daemon socket, then the same targeted command succeeded outside the sandbox with `BUILD SUCCESSFUL`. Fresh full-JVM logs show the estimator ran on current artifacts: aggregate dry-run rows across the generated full-JVM fixtures were `methods=20 helpers=626 trivialCandidates=0 fakeHelpers=626 multiRealHelpers=162 denseRouters=68 sparseRouters=558 helperInsns=176628 callSiteInsns=26918 minCallerGrowthInsns=149710`. Current obfusjack examples include `a/a.main([Ljava/lang/String;)V helpers=176 trivialCandidates=0 fakeHelpers=176 multiRealHelpers=25 denseRouters=9 sparseRouters=167 helperInsns=47294 callSiteInsns=7568 minCallerGrowthInsns=39726`. Hardening remains fail-closed: current full-JVM logs report `Control-flow generated helpers missing flow keys` with `keyed=0` for TEST, SnakeGame, evaluator, and obfusjack. Forbidden marker inspection of the same logs found no `MethodTooLarge`, fallback, skip-on-error, `translated=0`, native-library fallback, or static-decrypt marker. The evidence rejects trivial-island bypass priority for the current artifacts because every observed outlined island helper has at least one fake case (`trivialCandidates=0`, `fakeHelpers=626`); a future reduction route must target a different architecture path and still preserve live `flowkey` dependence.

- [ ] Subtask 7EB: Design key-dispatch update hardening with CFF flowkey, stack-trace, and thread-pool context.
  - Scope: after 7EA is completed, design an enhancement to the key-dispatch update path that incorporates live CFF `flowkey` state and explicitly accounts for stack-trace and thread-pool/asynchronous execution paths. This subtask must preserve hidden `long` key parameters, packed `Object[]` carriers, live method-entry key propagation, full CFF coverage, reflection/MethodHandle/lambda compatibility, and all existing key-dispatch ABI requirements. It must not introduce static decrypt, static key derivation, descriptor-only recomputation, self-canceling key updates, helper-layer fallback, original-bytecode fallback, thread-local static rescue keys, plaintext metadata, or transform skips.
  - Required evidence: user requested a midstream key-dispatch update enhancement that brings CFF flowkey plus stack-trace/thread-pool logic into scope. Implementation behavior is not yet fully specified, so before editing source this subtask must identify the exact current key-dispatch update invariant, the runtime paths affected by stack traces and thread-pool/asynchronous execution, and the concrete failure or missing-strength observation that justifies the enhancement.
  - Validation command/runtime target: before implementation, record the exact targeted JVM-obfuscation validation rows that exercise synchronous calls, exception/stack-trace paths, MethodHandle/lambda paths, and thread-pool/asynchronous execution under the same enabled transform set. Run only JVM-obfuscation related targeted validation; do not run the full test suite.
  - Completion criteria: do not start implementation until the missing behavior is clarified and the evidence chain identifies a generic architecture-level invariant. Accept only if live CFF `flowkey` remains semantically required on every updated path, generated code exposes no static decrypt/static key material, targeted JVM validation passes, forbidden marker scan remains clean, missing-flowkey rows remain `keyed=0`, and asynchronous/thread-pool paths preserve key correctness without fallback.
  - Evidence gathered so far: `JvmKeyDispatchPass` already establishes a method-entry key local, appends hidden `long` key parameters where JVM ABI allows, rewrites normal keyed invokes to load the live key local, rewrites reflective `Method.invoke` argument arrays to append the live key, and rewrites `LambdaMetafactory` invokedynamic descriptors so lambda objects can capture the live key at creation and pass it when invoked later. This covers many asynchronous lambda/thread-pool paths generically because the lambda's captured arguments include the key. External ABI callback slots remain different: `Runnable.run()`, `Callable.call()`, `Thread.run()`, inherited external overrides, constructors, class initializers, and `main` cannot simply receive a hidden long descriptor without violating JVM/external ABI. Existing targeted coverage includes direct/lambda/reflection entry-seed regression and full-JVM fixtures that print pool/virtual-thread paths, but no explicit stack-trace plus executor key-propagation invariant is recorded yet.
  - Clarified target: the enhancement must complete stack-trace/thread-pool key-dispatch paths at call sites by combining stack or thread-source analysis, live dynamic key input, and local class keytable/material dispatch. This must not mean ThreadLocal static rescue keys, static decrypt, static key recomputation, descriptor-only recomputation, runtime wrapper layers, generated helper classes, or external-ABI callback descriptor changes. The only acceptable route is a generic callsite/keytable design where any stack/thread source material is mixed with the live method/CFF flow key and class-local material before dispatch, with no self-canceling key update.

- [x] Subtask 7ED: Mix callsite source category into CFF key-transfer local keytable decoding.
  - Scope: strengthen existing generated key-transfer decoding by mixing callsite source category into the CFF dynamic-bound long decode seed. This targets LambdaMetafactory/async capture, reflective invocation, normal keyed calls, stack-trace, and exception/thread-related boundary calls as source categories for the local keytable/material dispatch. It must preserve the actual runtime long key value passed to the target, because callee entry-key correctness depends on it. It must not change external callback descriptors, create wrapper helper classes, use ThreadLocal rescue keys, introduce static decrypt/static key recomputation, alter CFF block construction, or create fallback behavior.
  - Required evidence: 7EC proves current full-JVM artifacts contain relevant boundaries (`lambdaMetaRewrites=33`, `asyncCalls=7`, `stackTraceCalls=2`, `reflectiveInvokes=6`, `normalKeyedCalls=269`). Existing CFF already rewrites generated key loads through `emitDynamicBoundDecodedLong`, which decodes the same raw incoming key from live method key, guard/path/block state, and class-local keytable/material masks. The missing enhancement is source-category binding in that local keytable dispatch seed.
  - Validation command/runtime target: compile affected transform classes and run only the same JVM-obfuscation targeted validation set. Inspect full-JVM logs for context census, hardening `keyed=0`, forbidden markers, and successful runtime. Do not run the full test suite.

  - Rejection evidence: implemented source-category seed mixing in `ControlFlowFlatteningPass` by classifying LambdaMetafactory/async carriers, reflective invocation/lookup, async thread-pool APIs, stack-trace calls, and exception calls, then XORing that source seed into every `emitDynamicBoundDecodedLong` key-transfer decode seed. This preserved the runtime long key value and did not add ThreadLocal, wrapper classes, helper layers, external ABI descriptor changes, static decrypt, or fallback logic. Manual compilation passed, but the targeted JVM-obfuscation validation failed while writing the fresh obfusjack full-JVM artifact: `org.objectweb.asm.MethodTooLargeException: Method too large: a/a.main ([Ljava/lang/String;)V`, with largest-method diagnostics `65888 bytes estimated main([Ljava/lang/String;)V`, `64523 bytes estimated ei([Ljava/lang/Object;)V`, `64389 bytes estimated oa([Ljava/lang/Object;)V`, `61903 bytes estimated jb([Ljava/lang/Object;)V`, and `61772 bytes estimated pa([Ljava/lang/Object;)V`. This violates 7ED completion criteria, so the implementation was reverted. The revert kept 7EC census only. Post-revert manual compilation passed, and a fresh targeted rerun with `--rerun-tasks` for the same five JVM-obfuscation test classes passed with `BUILD SUCCESSFUL` and `19 actionable tasks: 19 executed`; no full test suite was run. Fresh post-revert logs still show the 7EC aggregate context census `methods=149 indySites=98 lambdaMetaSites=35 indyRewrites=33 lambdaMetaRewrites=33 normalKeyedCalls=269 reflectiveLookups=5 reflectiveInvokes=6 asyncCalls=7 stackTraceCalls=2 exceptionCalls=40`, hardening remains `keyed=0` for all full-JVM fixtures, and the forbidden marker scan is clean. Therefore direct in-caller source-category expansion is blocked by method-size headroom, not by key-correctness proof.

- [x] Subtask 7EE: Design a size-safe key-transfer source-mix route after 7ED method-size rejection.
  - Scope: define the next implementation route for stack/thread source analysis plus live dynamic key plus local keytable dispatch without growing protected caller methods past verifier limits. Candidate routes must preserve the exact runtime key value and move or compress source-category decoding outside the large protected caller body only if the moved path remains live-key/keytable dependent and is not a helper-layer fallback.
  - Required evidence: 7ED proves direct caller-side source-category seed expansion fails `MethodTooLarge` on obfusjack. 7EC proves the relevant boundary surface exists. 7EA/7DW/7DZ prove naive inlining/bypass routes are already method-size sensitive.
  - Validation command/runtime target: design/audit first; if implemented later, compile affected transforms and run only the JVM-obfuscation targeted validation set. Do not run the full test suite.
  - Completion criteria: record a generic architecture-level route or reject the route with exact evidence. Do not implement unless the design includes method-size bounds, live `flowkey` dependency, class-local keytable/material dependency, no static decrypt/static key recomputation, no external ABI breakage, and no fallback behavior.
  - Completion evidence: accepted as design-only. The direct 7ED approach was rejected because even bytecode-shape-preserving seed changes can change immediate constant encodings and push obfusjack's already-large caller over the 64KB verifier limit. Therefore the next valid implementation cannot expand or perturb every protected caller-side `emitDynamicBoundDecodedLong` site. The size-safe route is a materialized CFF key-transfer decode path: register per-key-transfer rows in the existing class-owned object-array/keytable material surface, include source-category material in those rows, and replace large inline dynamic-bound decode at selected generated key-transfer sites with a compact call to a CFF generated transfer-decode helper that takes live method key, guard/path/block state, row id/material cursor, and returns the exact same raw incoming long key. This route preserves runtime key correctness because the returned long remains `incomingRawForCanonical(targetSeed)`, while decode remains bound to live `flowkey`/method key and class-local material. It avoids external ABI descriptor changes, ThreadLocal/static rescue keys, wrapper classes, and fallback behavior. Open implementation prerequisites: define the key-transfer material row layout, prove helper call bytecode is smaller than the inline decode in method-size-bound callers, ensure helper itself is not per-site duplicated, and validate that added helper/material init does not reintroduce `MethodTooLarge`.

- [x] Subtask 7EF: Implement materialized CFF key-transfer decode helper for source-mix boundaries.
  - Scope: implement the 7EE size-safe route by moving source-category-aware key-transfer decode material into class-owned object-array/keytable rows and emitting a compact generated CFF transfer-decode helper call at key-transfer sites where method-size headroom is tight. The helper must return the exact incoming raw key expected by existing callee entry-key mixing, and must be driven by live method key plus guard/path/block state. It must not add external ABI descriptors, ThreadLocal keys, wrapper classes, plaintext source metadata, static decrypt, static key recomputation, fallback/original bytecode behavior, or CFF coverage reduction.
  - Required evidence: 7ED direct inline source mix failed `MethodTooLarge`; 7EE defines the materialized decode route; 7EC identifies concrete async/lambda/reflect/stack/exception boundary surfaces.
  - Validation command/runtime target: compile affected transforms and run only the JVM-obfuscation targeted validation set. Inspect helper/material counts, method-size diagnostics, context census, hardening `keyed=0`, forbidden markers, and runtime success. Do not run the full test suite.

  - Completion evidence: accepted. Implemented a class-local generated `__neko_cff_kxfer$...` helper with descriptor `(JIII[Ljava/lang/Object;I)I`. Each helper decodes one 32-bit key-transfer word from the existing class-owned `Object[]` carrier and token material rows, then XORs a fold of the live method key. Call sites still assemble the final 64-bit incoming raw key locally with `I2L`, `LSHL`, `LAND`, and `LOR`, preserving the strong-entry regression invariant that the callee seed is assembled at the callsite. The high and low word material rows are registered through the existing token material path; their material seed includes source-category data derived from the surrounding LambdaMetafactory/indy, reflective invoke/lookup, async/thread-pool, stack-trace, or exception boundary call. Runtime key values are unchanged: the helper returns the exact high/low words of `incomingRawForCanonical(targetSeed)`, so existing callee entry-key mixing remains compatible. The implementation does not add ThreadLocal state, wrapper classes, external ABI descriptors, plaintext source metadata, fallback paths, original-bytecode rescue, or static decrypt/static key recomputation. Manual `neko-transforms` compilation passed. A first helper version returning a full `long` failed `CffStrongEntrySeedRegressionTest` because callsite long assembly disappeared; it was corrected to return one int word so callsite assembly remains visible. Fresh targeted JVM-obfuscation validation with `--rerun-tasks` passed for `JvmStringObfuscationIntegrationTest`, `JvmInvokeDynamicObfuscationIntegrationTest`, `ControlFlowFlatteningAlgebraicAuditTest`, `CffStrongEntrySeedRegressionTest`, and `JvmFullObfuscationPerfTest` with `BUILD SUCCESSFUL` and `19 actionable tasks: 19 executed`; no full test suite was run. Current context census remains `methods=149 indySites=98 lambdaMetaSites=35 indyRewrites=33 lambdaMetaRewrites=33 normalKeyedCalls=269 reflectiveLookups=5 reflectiveInvokes=6 asyncCalls=7 stackTraceCalls=2 exceptionCalls=40`. Generated maps show `__neko_cff_kxfer` material helpers are present: `88` total across current full-JVM maps and `18` in obfusjack. Hardening remains fail-closed with `Control-flow generated helpers missing flow keys` reporting `keyed=0` for TEST, SnakeGame, evaluator, and obfusjack. Forbidden marker scan over the same fresh logs found no `MethodTooLarge`, fallback, skip-on-error, `translated=0`, native-library fallback, or static-decrypt marker. Generated helper API after this route is obfusjack `methods=390 fields=18`, TEST `methods=319 fields=34`, evaluator `methods=242 fields=29`, and SnakeGame `methods=97 fields=7`; this is an accepted tradeoff for completing the stack/thread source-mix key-transfer materialization without caller method-size failure.

- [x] Subtask 7EJ: Scope CFF island-dispatch shared/materialized prototype.
  - Scope: define a bounded prototype for the remaining `__neko_cff$` island-dispatch helper surface. This is not permission to implement a table-driven dispatcher yet. The prototype must first specify material row layout, dispatch mode, caller growth estimate, helper size estimate, live key dependency, fake/poison/result semantics, and validation rows.
  - Required evidence: 7EI proves all smaller routes are closed and remaining helper surface is `__neko_cff$`. 7DV/7DW/7DX already warn that this is hot-path and method-size sensitive.
  - Validation command/runtime target: planning/audit first. If later implemented, run only JVM-obfuscation targeted validation unless explicitly instructed otherwise; do not run the full test suite.
  - Completion criteria: produce a prototype boundary that is generic, method-size-safe, full-strength CFF preserving, live-flowkey dependent, and free of fallback/static decrypt/static key recomputation.
  - Completion evidence: accepted as design-only. The remaining `__neko_cff$` island-dispatch helpers cannot be reduced by exact-body sharing, trivial bypass, caller inline, init chunking, or key-transfer helper sharing. A valid prototype must therefore be staged in two parts before any semantic replacement is attempted. Stage 1 is a dry-run estimator: for each outlined island helper, record caller method size, generated helper size, island real-block count, fake-case count, dense/sparse result-router mode, dispatch-case count, result-token count, bounce-token presence, poison path presence, and current helper bytecode size. It must compute a projected caller delta and a projected shared-helper/material row size without modifying emitted bytecode. Stage 2 is a material-layout proof: define rows for real dispatch tokens, fake dispatch tokens, fake bounce metadata, result token encoding, dense/sparse mode, poison behavior, and `outLocal` transition writes, while proving that every dispatch decision and every returned key remains driven by live method key plus guard/path/block/pc/domain state and class-owned object-array/keytable material. Direct implementation is blocked until both stages prove method-size safety and hot-path viability. Rejected shortcuts remain closed: deleting dead transition wrapper code does not change artifacts; inlining helpers moves size back into protected callers; table-probing shared dispatch without a hot-path gate risks runtime regression; static descriptor/seed recomputation violates dynamic flowkey requirements.

- [x] Subtask 7EP: Prove material row layout for CFF fake/poison key-step and bounce semantics.
  - Scope: define and validate a non-semantic material layout for the parts that block 7EO: seed/role-dependent `emitStepKeys`, fake-case bounce routing, domain writes, dense/sparse result token writes, and poison hard-fail behavior. This proof must show how a shared helper can execute the same dynamic key updates from live key/control state and class-owned material rows without self-canceling key logic, static seed recomputation, fallback, or reduced fake coverage.
  - Required evidence: source path evidence from current island helper generation: real cases only call `finishOutlinedDispatchReturn`, but fake cases call `emitStepKeys(..., EdgeRole.FAKE)` and `emitOutlinedFakeCaseBounce(...)`; poison calls `emitStepKeys(..., EdgeRole.POISON)` before throwing. 7EN row counts are not enough to implement these paths because they do not yet encode the key-step operation selectors, source-local selectors, second-step/method-key update selector, bounce domain target, or masked result behavior.
  - Validation command/runtime target: source/audit first; if instrumentation is added, compile affected transform code and run only JVM-obfuscation targeted validation. Do not run the full test suite.
  - Completion criteria: accept only if the proof records concrete row fields for fake/poison step operations and bounce/result writes, proves every field is decoded from live key/control/material state, and decides whether 7EO can proceed as one semantic implementation without weakening CFF fake/poison coverage.
  - Completion evidence: accepted as source-proof only; no production bytecode was changed and no tests were required. Exact blocking source paths were inspected. `emitStepKeys` derives the first key destination/source, tiny int update operation, optional second key update, and optional method-key update from `roleSeed`. `emitStepMethodKeyTiny` has four long-key update modes. `emitOutlinedFakeCaseBounce` has four bounce order/predicate modes from `(seed >>> 37) & 3`, updates pc/method key/domain, and then calls `finishOutlinedDispatchReturn` with the fake bounce token. Poison executes `emitStepKeys(..., EdgeRole.POISON)` before throwing. Therefore 7EO cannot legally reduce fake/poison paths to real-result rows or dead poison throws.
  - Required shared-dispatch material rows for 7EO are now defined. Common case row: `kind`, encrypted dispatch token cursor, result/bounce row cursor, and per-row live-key/material salt. Real result row: result token, dense/sparse result mode, result-route mask seed material, outLocal write mode, and live method-key fold material. Fake step row: role ordinal, first destination index, first source index, first tiny-op mode, first tiny-op constant, second-step presence, second destination/source index or method-key-update flag, second tiny-op/method-key-op mode, second constant, and step material salt. Fake bounce row: bounce order mode, optional predicate seed material, target pc token material, target guard/path/block/method-key material, target domain token material, bounce result token, dense/sparse result mode, and outLocal write mode. Poison row: poison role step row plus hard-fail marker; no success outLocal write is allowed. All fields must be stored in the class-owned object-array/material surface and decoded with live key/guard/path/block/pc/domain state, not recomputed from static seeds or descriptors.
  - 7EO can proceed as one semantic implementation only if the shared helper implements a small material interpreter for these row types. It must use the existing live-key dynamic arithmetic for step operations, preserve fake bounce and poison behavior, and keep result-router compatibility by writing the same outLocal layout consumed by the current caller router. The dependency state recorded under 7EO is resolved by this row proof, but 7EO itself remains unimplemented.

- [x] Subtask 7ES: Implement minimal CFF material interpreter for step operations only.
  - Scope: implement the first semantic slice of the 7EO interpreter: a shared generated helper that decodes materialized step rows and executes the same first tiny update, optional second tiny update, and optional method-key tiny update currently produced by `emitStepKeys`. This slice must not replace island dispatch yet; it should be used only where behavior can be proven equivalent, or remain as a generated helper with targeted self-use proof before full dispatch replacement.
  - Required evidence: 7ER proves exact operation counts and bounded maxima. `emitStepKeys` is a common prerequisite for fake and poison rows; isolating it first reduces interpreter risk before materializing bounce/result writes.
  - Validation command/runtime target: compile affected transform code and run only JVM-obfuscation targeted validation with `--rerun-tasks`. Do not run the full test suite.
  - Completion criteria: accept only if step-row helper semantics are exercised on fresh artifacts, targeted validation passes, hardening remains `keyed=0`, no helper fallback/static decrypt/static-key exposure appears, and no CFF fake/poison coverage is reduced.
  - Dependency state: blocked until 7ET defines a compact step-material storage surface. 7ER reports `fakeStepRows + poisonStepRows = 1872` across the current four full-JVM artifacts. Reusing existing token material with one token-material row per step field would require many more than 16384 token rows for the current proof set and would risk exhausting `TOKEN_MATERIAL_TABLE_SIZE` before the actual island interpreter is implemented.
  - Implementation state: wiring in progress. The intended implementation keeps the callsite ABI dynamic: the island helper passes live method key, guard key, path key, block key, class-owned material carrier, row id, and transition-output scratch into the generated step-material helper. The helper is the only place allowed to decode and execute the material row; no static method-entry key recomputation, descriptor-only recomputation, original bytecode fallback, or reduced fake/poison coverage is allowed.
  - Completion evidence: accepted. Implemented a dedicated class-owned step-material slot backed by packed `long[]` rows, a generated `__neko_cff_step$` interpreter helper, chunked `__neko_cff_step_init$` material init helpers, and island helper fake/poison callsite wiring. The helper ABI is dynamic: callers pass live method key, guard key, path key, block key, class-owned material carrier, material row id, and transition-output scratch; it returns the updated method key and writes updated guard/path/block through the scratch array. Row words `0..4` are not read as plaintext: they are stored masked and decoded inside the helper from a runtime base computed from live key/control state plus row-local mask words `5..7`. Selectors/constants therefore travel through local keytable material dispatch and live-flowkey-dependent decode, not through static method-entry key recomputation, descriptor-only recomputation, fallback, or original-bytecode rescue.
  - Runtime proof: `ControlFlowFlatteningAlgebraicAuditTest` now loads the freshly obfuscated `CffAuditShapes` artifact, locates the generated step-material helper by descriptor `(JIII[Ljava/lang/Object;I[J)J`, fetches the generated class-owned `Object[]` carrier, invokes material row `0`, asserts the helper executes a materialized row, then invokes the same row with nonzero live method key/guard/path/block and asserts the result changes. This proves the generated helper executes against fresh artifact material and that dispatch output depends on live key/control state.
  - Fresh validation: manual `neko-transforms` compilation passed. A focused `ControlFlowFlatteningAlgebraicAuditTest` run passed with `BUILD SUCCESSFUL in 5s`. The full targeted JVM-obfuscation gate only then passed with `BUILD SUCCESSFUL in 17s` and `19 actionable tasks: 19 executed`; no full test suite was run. XML rows are clean: `JvmFullObfuscationPerfTest` `tests="1" skipped="0" failures="0" errors="0"`, `ControlFlowFlatteningAlgebraicAuditTest` `tests="2" skipped="0" failures="0" errors="0"`, `JvmInvokeDynamicObfuscationIntegrationTest` `tests="1" skipped="0" failures="0" errors="0"`, `JvmStringObfuscationIntegrationTest` `tests="2" skipped="0" failures="0" errors="0"`, and `CffStrongEntrySeedRegressionTest` `tests="1" skipped="0" failures="0" errors="0"`. Marker scans over the fresh targeted test results found no `MethodTooLarge`, fallback, skip-on-error, `translated=0`, native-library fallback, original-bytecode rescue, static-decrypt marker, verifier error, SIGSEGV, or SIGABRT. Hardening rows observed in the fresh target logs remain fail-closed with `keyed=0`.

- [x] Subtask 7ET: Prove compact CFF step-material slot capacity and cinit pressure.
  - Scope: define a class-owned object-array slot for compact step-material rows independent of token material. This is a design/proof subtask unless a non-semantic estimator is added. It must estimate row width, total rows, packed long count, init helper chunking, and worst-case `<clinit>` pressure for the current artifacts. It must not change generated runtime behavior, helper ABI, CFF block construction, dispatch semantics, or key propagation.
  - Required evidence: 7ES cannot safely use existing token material because 7ER step operation counts are too large for field-per-token-row encoding. The compact slot must store operation selectors and constants densely while still being decoded under live key/control/material state when 7ES implements the helper.
  - Validation command/runtime target: source/proof first; if instrumentation is added, compile affected transform code and run only JVM-obfuscation targeted validation. Do not run the full test suite.
  - Completion criteria: accept only if the plan records concrete row words, current total rows, projected packed long count, worst-class row count, cinit chunking strategy, and why this avoids token material exhaustion and MethodTooLarge while preserving future live-key decode requirements.
  - Completion evidence: accepted as source/log proof only; no production bytecode changed. The compact step row will use 8 int words packed as 4 long stores per row. Proposed row words: selector word for first-destination/source/op, second-kind/destination/source/op, method-key-op, role/hard-fail flags; first tiny constant; second tiny constant; method-key constant high; method-key constant low; live-decode mask add; live-decode mask multiply; live-decode shift/digest. The row is stored in a new class-owned object-array slot as packed `long[]`, not in token material. Future 7ES decode must combine these words with live key/guard/path/block state and the local material mask words, so it is not static seed recomputation or static decrypt.
  - Fresh 7ER log projection: SnakeGame rows `181`, TEST rows `533`, evaluator rows `353`, obfusjack rows `805`, total rows `1872`. With the selected 8-word row width this is `724`, `2132`, `1412`, and `3220` packed long stores respectively, `7488` long stores total across the four artifacts. Worst method has `fakeStepRows=327` and `poisonStepRows=176`. A 512-long-store cinit chunk size yields worst obfusjack step material init helper count `ceil(3220/512)=7`; TEST needs `ceil(2132/512)=5`. This is smaller than current token-material init surfaces and avoids the `TOKEN_MATERIAL_TABLE_SIZE=16384` exhaustion risk that field-per-token-row encoding would create.
  - Route decision: 7ES is unblocked only if it adds a dedicated step-material slot and init helpers using this compact packed layout. Reusing token material per field is rejected. The helper must hard-fail or not be used if the step material table is exhausted; no fallback/static seed path is allowed.

- [x] Subtask 7FU: Add callsite stack/thread-source dynamic keytable dispatch.
  - Scope: implement the user's clarified key-dispatch update after 7FT: at eligible callsites, derive a runtime source signal from stack provenance and/or thread/thread-pool provenance, combine that signal with the live dynamically passed flow key, and dispatch through the caller/class-local keytable. This must be a generic JVM obfuscation surface, not a sample-specific rule. It must not statically decrypt material, expose raw flow keys, introduce descriptor-only recomputation, ThreadLocal rescue keys, fallback, helper classes, reduced CFF coverage, or self-canceling key logic.
  - Dependency reason: 7FO installed minimum-cost thread identity bucket dispatch on the hot CFF island material decode path and explicitly rejected stack-source-on-every-island-decode for performance. The user's clarification requires stack/thread-source analysis at callsites, not a hot-loop replacement for CFF island material decode. Therefore the next implementation must attach stack/thread provenance to callsite key dispatch where it can be amortized and then bind that provenance to the live dynamic key plus local keytable row selection.
  - Required evidence: before editing source, identify the concrete generated callsite path that already receives the live flow key and indexes class-owned keytable/material rows. The evidence must prove the selected path can consume stack/thread provenance without static seed material and without changing JVM ABI-visible descriptors except the planned hidden-key/internal generated surface. If stack trace collection on a hot path regresses runtime, the implementation must either bound/amortize that source at the callsite or reject that route with exact runtime evidence instead of moving it into CFF island hot-loop dispatch.

Do not run the full test suite.

  - Rejected evidence: the first 7FU implementation computed thread-source material directly in the original method callsite before every `__neko_cff$` island helper call. The selected path is now `__neko_cff$` helper entry computes a runtime source from `Thread.currentThread`, `System.identityHashCode(thread)`, live method-entry `long` key, guard/path/block, pc, domain, and the encoded island material cursor, stores it in a helper local, and every real material read passes that source into the shared `__neko_cff_imat$` helper. `__neko_cff_imat$` ABI changed from `(JIII[Ljava/lang/Object;II)I` to `(JIII[Ljava/lang/Object;III)I`; it no longer reads thread/stack provenance itself and uses the passed runtime source to select the class-local island material keytable bucket before applying live key/class-key material decode.
